    `1.014s +/- 0.036`.
  - Symbol profile was available on this host (`perf_event_paranoid=1`).
    LPUSH P16/C50/n2M profile rows kept the command-packet/runtime/output
    surface visible: `execute_plain_keyed_values_write_borrowed`
    `6.01%` total / `2.10%` self, `TcpStream::write` `4.56%`,
    `UnixStream::write` `4.42%`, `__send` `4.29%`,
    `parse_command_args_borrowed_into` `3.91%` / `2.55%` self,
    `plain_borrowed_default_key_write_allows` `3.05%` / `2.36%` self,
    time reads around `2.2-2.4%`, `__memmove_avx_unaligned_erms`
    `2.02%`, `process_buffered_frames` `1.95%` / `1.05%` self,
    `ListValue::push_front` `1.78%` / `1.13%` self, and
    `Store::lpush` `1.68%` / `1.59%` self.
- Candidate rejected:
  - Moved the existing `SADD | LPUSH | RPUSH` borrowed keyed-values matcher in
    `parse_borrowed_multibulk_action` ahead of unrelated INCR/DECR/APPEND
    probes, so LPUSH reaches the same runtime fast path after fewer failed
    matcher checks.
  - This was a command-packet routing/order-only trial. It did not add a parser,
    did not change the runtime/store/output handlers, and did not alter command
    bytes, key/value slices, response type, suppression logic, or fallback paths.
- Behavior proof while applied:
  - Raw TCP golden covered `DEL`, multi-value `LPUSH`, `LRANGE` ordering,
    `RPUSH`, `SADD` duplicate handling, `SCARD`, `CLIENT REPLY SKIP/ON`,
    another `LPUSH`, and `QUIT`.
  - Input SHA256:
    `b616e89b3d03d365c042ec2383a73c987a7dd43d54ce88c091a82d8ec7645068`
    (`401` bytes).
  - Baseline and candidate output SHA256 both:
    `c4a2d062abdffc07a2dc90066d20a53a049cffc259e708d0556a095fac0c5ade`
    (`122` bytes, byte-equal).
  - Ordering/tie-breaking/floating-point/RNG proof: matcher order only decides
    which mutually exclusive existing fast-path predicate is tried first. The
    successful LPUSH/RPUSH/SADD path, value order, list/set mutations, integer
    reply bytes, reply suppression, and fallback semantics are identical; there
    are no floating-point or RNG paths in the candidate.
- Benchmarks:
  - Candidate standalone LPUSH P16/C50/n1M:
    `1.030s +/- 0.042`, slower than the saved current-main baseline
    `1.014s +/- 0.036`.
  - Paired same-window LPUSH P16/C50/n1M:
    current `996.9ms +/- 22.0ms`, candidate `1.003s +/- 0.034s`;
    current `1.01x +/- 0.04` faster than candidate.
- Gates:
  - RCH `cargo build --release -p fr-server` passed for baseline and candidate,
    both with only the pre-existing `fr-command` `limit_offset`/`limit_count`
    warnings and `fr-runtime` `PlainKeyedPopCmd::is_zpop` warning.
  - `cargo fmt -p fr-server -- --check` passed while the candidate was applied.
- Decision:
  - Reject `frankenredis-par0e` under Score>=2.0. Impact `0.0` x Confidence
    `4.0` / Effort `0.5` = `0.0`.
  - Production source hunk was removed before commit; evidence retained under
    `artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-coralox-pass165/`.
- Next route:
  - Do not repeat borrowed matcher ordering/router micro-tuning, exact LPUSH
    parsers, direct reply encoding, write-buffer spare capacity, or list-front
    storage/capacity variants. LPUSH is now a small (`1.04x`) flat residual and
    the profile is spread across parser/gate/timing/output/store.
  - Follow the ready deeper primitive from the rebased tracker:
    `frankenredis-e82wj` if its output/syscall profile remains top-ranked, or
    the key-layout bead if it ranks higher. Require a fresh non-list profile
    before returning to `fr-server` matcher order.
- Artifacts: `artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-coralox-pass165/`.
- Verdict: REJECTED / NO SOURCE KEPT.

  focused COW/listpack tests passed:
  `list_value_clone_shares_large_deque_until_mutation`,

  `copy_large_deque_list_mutations_are_isolated`, and

- Score: Impact `4.95` x Confidence `0.95` / Effort `2.0` = `2.35`, keep.

- Started: 2026-06-11T09:59:00-04:00.

  `Arc` and use `Arc::make_mut` on writes. Normal unique list pushes stay
  pointer-fast; COPY/clone becomes an O(1) refcount bump; the first mutation of
  a shared post-COPY list performs the required isolation clone.

  quicklist-shaped list improved from `655.3ms ±25.9ms` to `139.4ms ±4.9ms`
  (4.70x). The measured COPY loop improved from `1812.4` to `16797.7` ops/s
  (9.27x).

  destination LSET, LPOP/RPOP, and OBJECT ENCODING matched exactly:
  `839623b8168bcd72f111ffbd9e895d241395aa8cd5190a7b62c62ec6343d5286`;
  stable behavior JSON matched with SHA-256
  `274ed9483af91fc8476aa452cf123d0e112a779ef39c4706f638266d211953fd`.
- Gates: focused `fr-store` COW isolation and byte-exact listpack tests passed;
  `cargo check -p fr-store --all-targets` passed with pre-existing test
  warnings; `cargo clippy -p fr-store --lib -- -D warnings` passed;
  `cargo fmt -p fr-store -- --check` passed; `git diff --check` passed. UBS

### Pass 113: reject nonnumeric SET canonicalization bypass for `frankenredis-ohsk5.11`

- Started: 2026-06-10T00:18:00-04:00.
- Closed: 2026-06-10T00:34:00-04:00.
- Bead: `frankenredis-ohsk5.11`.
- Profile-backed target: current `origin/main` `46b3a9b3a` after the direct
  borrowed SET packet parser. Baseline SET/P16/C50/1M was
  `906.2 ms +/- 34.2 ms`. Fresh SET/P16/C50/3M profile reached
  `1311240.5925841355 ops/sec`, p50 `569us`, p95 `884us`, p99 `1216us`,
  3008 samples, 0 lost. Top relevant rows were
  `fr_store::canonical_string_value_from_slice` `10.46%` self,
  `Runtime::execute_plain_set_borrowed` `0.88%` self / `4.73%` children,
  `Store::set_plain_borrowed` `1.68%` self / `2.54%` children,
  and writer-thread `__send` at `19.76%` and `18.66%` children.
- Candidate rejected before source edits: a nonnumeric SET payload bypass ahead
  of Redis integer canonicalization. `fr-bench` with `--datasize 3` writes
  nonnumeric payloads only for request indices `0..99`; from `100` onward,
  `value_for_request` returns the decimal suffix because it is at least as long
  as the template. For SET/P16/C50/3M, the bypass would cover about
  `5,000 / 3,000,000 = 0.17%` of requests.
- Prior art checked: pass105 first-byte integer-candidate gate, pass106 borrowed
  `SmallStr` canonicalization, pass107 lazy borrowed SET integer classification,
  and pass110 positive short integer parsing were all proof-clean or compile-clean
  but failed the benchmark/score gate. This pass therefore did not repeat that
  micro-family.
- Isomorphism proof: no production source changed. Ordering, tie-breaking,
  floating-point behavior, RNG, expiry, key policy, reply bytes, object encoding,
  and digest semantics are unchanged by the no-diff rejection.
- Score: Impact `0.2` x Confidence `4.0` / Effort `1.0` = `0.8`, below the
  `>=2.0` keep gate.
- Evidence retained under
  `artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-ohsk5/pass113/`.
- Next route: stop SET integer-classification variants. The pass113 profile
  exposes a larger writer-thread `__send` surface; pass114 should attack one
  safe writer-side syscall/buffer coalescing primitive, preserving per-client
  reply order and byte-identical transcripts.

### Pass 109: reject read/parse ownership boundary for `frankenredis-zhphm`

- Started: 2026-06-09T22:47:49-04:00.
- Closed: 2026-06-09T22:58:00-04:00.
- Bead: `frankenredis-zhphm.6`.

  `1.133711212s`, over 1M requests.

  `core::str::from_utf8` `0.24%`.
- Decision: reject bounded read-worker / parse-worker ownership transfer. The
  measured read/parse surface is real but too small for the queueing,
  synchronization, and ordering proof burden.
- Candidate trial: reusable `Vec<&[u8]>` for borrowed argv slices was attempted
  as the only source lever, but `cargo check -p fr-server --all-targets` rejected
  it with `E0502`; safe reuse of references across event-loop turns widens the
  `conn.read_buf` borrow even with explicit clear boundaries. The hunk was
  removed and no production source change was retained.
- Isomorphism proof: ordering, tie-breaking, floating-point, and RNG are
  unchanged because the committed state has no production code diff. Golden
  output proof is vacuous for this rejected compile-only candidate; no candidate
  binary exists.
- Score: read/parse offload Impact `1.0` x Confidence `2.0` / Effort `4.0` =
  `0.5`; borrowed argv scratch reuse score `0` because it fails the compile
  gate. Reject under the `>=2.0` keep gate.
- Evidence retained under
  `artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-zhphm/pass109/`.
- Next route: pass110 should attack a different command-packet/layout primitive
  that avoids storing borrowed slices across loop state, or reprofile into
  `fr_store::canonical_string_value_from_slice` if it remains top.

### Pass 95: `frankenredis-ohsk5.6` fr-server foldhash event-loop maps rejected

- Profile-backed target: pass95 SET P16/1M profile on current head
  `c85f25527` showed `SipHasher::write` at `12.62%` self in
  `frankenredis`, with write-flush children `22.11%`,

  and smaller store/parser/hash rows. Candidate scope was restricted to
  `fr-server` event-loop maps/sets (`clients`, token registries,
  blocked-wake indexes, paused/deferred/write/closing sets, and sentinel
  hello subscriptions) by switching those surfaces from std SipHash to
  `foldhash::quality`.
- Isolation: created clean scratch worktrees at the same parent commit for
  baseline and candidate. Candidate contained only the `fr-server`/`Cargo.lock`
  foldhash hunk; the unrelated stream parity work on shared `main` was excluded
  from the benchmark comparison.
- Behavior proof:
  - exact RESP transcript comparator matched baseline and candidate byte-for-byte
    with SHA-256
    `cd37cbcdc1c44b04bcd11c2644c6ed0233cbc87eca53c9edfab159e9d8a748f3`;
  - ordering and per-client FIFO are unchanged because command parsing and
    `write_buf` append order are untouched, blocked-key FIFO remains in
    `VecDeque`, timeout ordering remains `BinaryHeap`, and hash iteration order
    was already not Redis-observable for these registries;
  - tie-breaking, floating-point, and RNG are N/A for this lever; expiry math and
    reply bytes were unchanged.
- Validation/build notes:
  - `rch exec -- env CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/tmp/codex-fr-ohsk56-baseline-target cargo
    build --profile release-perf -p fr-server -p fr-bench` passed locally after
    RCH had no admissible workers;
  - candidate build selected `vmi1153651` but remote preflight failed with
    `Syntax error: newline unexpected`, then local fallback passed:
    `cargo build --profile release-perf -p fr-server -p fr-bench`;
  - a verification subagent audited invariants and flagged the non-semantic
    security tradeoff that `BlockedWakeIndex.by_key` hashes client-controlled
    Redis keys, so foldhash would reduce HashDoS resistance versus SipHash.
- Benchmarks:
  - paired SET P16/300k: baseline `0.5304333017s +/- 0.0144884337`,
    candidate `0.5289788372s +/- 0.0189245460`, candidate only
    `1.00x +/- 0.05`;
  - reversed SET P16/1M: candidate `1.6703246832s +/- 0.0468934548`,
    baseline `1.6731883738s +/- 0.1010037626`, candidate only
    `1.00x +/- 0.07`.
- Decision: reject under Score>=2.0. Impact `0`, confidence `4`, effort `1`,
  score `0`. The production foldhash hunk was removed, `frankenredis-ohsk5.6`
  was closed rejected, and evidence is retained under
  `artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-ohsk5.6/`.
- Next route: stop event-loop hasher swaps. Pass 96 should re-profile current
  pushed main and attack a different primitive class, preferably reply/output
  batching or keyspace layout/fingerprint reduction only if fresh profile
  evidence supports it.

  `PackedStrMap::locate` `3.92%`, `parse_command_args_borrowed_into` `3.11%`,
  `HashFieldMap::insert` `2.77%`, foldhash `Vec<u8>` hashing `2.26%`,
  `Store::hset` `2.13%`, `__memcmp_avx2_movbe` `1.68%`, and
  `execute_plain_hset_borrowed` `1.65%`.
- Lever tested: borrowed HSET mutation capsule for the runtime borrowed fast
  path. The candidate added a `Store::hset_borrowed` path and switched
  `execute_plain_hset_borrowed` to call it, avoiding the generic
  `Store::internal_entry` path for borrowed HSET while leaving generic HSET and
  packed field lookup semantics unchanged.
- Behavior proof while applied: RCH
  `cargo test -p fr-store hset_borrowed_matches_generic_hset_observables -- --nocapture`
  passed. The test compared generic HSET and borrowed HSET over new-field,
  overwrite, insertion order, LFU/object frequency, hash encoding promotion,
  dirty count, digest mutation count, and wrong-type behavior.
- Benchmarks:
  - baseline HSET P16/300k before edit: `0.5983109633s +/- 0.0143103008`;
  - paired HSET P16/300k baseline `0.5880823822s +/- 0.0290218240`,
    candidate `0.5508260319s +/- 0.0284958077`, candidate `1.07x +/- 0.08`;
  - reversed HSET P16/1M candidate `1.7757010856s +/- 0.1240665869`,
    baseline `1.7038294932s +/- 0.0385267296`, baseline `1.04x +/- 0.08`.
- Decision: reject under Score>=2.0. The longer reversed run flipped against the
  candidate. The production source hunk and candidate-only test were removed;
  evidence is retained under `artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-ohsk5.4/`.
- Next route: stop HSET mutation-capsule micro-levers. Attack a deeper
  safe-Rust keyspace/fingerprint layout only if hashing/memcmp/internal-entry
  costs dominate across multiple P16 workloads, or a batch command-packet
  primitive if broad dispatch/parser/runtime metadata dominates collectively.

### Pass 90: `frankenredis-ohsk5.2` HSET packed-hash single-locate API rejected

- Profile-backed target: pass89 HSET profile remained the evidence source:

  HSET can derive the new-field bit from the same packed-record lookup used for
  insertion. This was the deeper version of pass89's call-site-only

  `contains_key` scan for existing fields and avoided computing a discarded old
  value for HSET.

    focused tests.

    metamorphic hash cases.
  - RCH `cargo clippy -p fr-store --all-targets -- -D warnings` passed.
  - `rustfmt --edition 2024 --check crates/fr-store/src/packed_set.rs` passed;
    crate-level fmt remains blocked by an unrelated committed `lib.rs:22144`
    rustfmt hunk.
- Benchmarks:

    `1.73510668626s +/- 0.023866332216318432`, baseline
    `1.8043301090100001s +/- 0.03351858216091114`; summary `1.04x +/- 0.02`.
  - Baseline-first HSET P16/1M: baseline

    `1.7543096089199997s +/- 0.042859135068909635`; summary `1.02x +/- 0.03`.

### Pass 89: `frankenredis-ohsk5.1` HSET packed-hash single-probe rejected

- Profile-backed target: pass89 re-profile showed HSET as the largest current
  P16 Redis gap (`511717.53 ops/sec` vs Redis `730918.21 ops/sec`, ratio
  `0.7001`, p99 `10679us` vs `2031us`). The focused HSET P16/1M profile
  recorded `596739.56 ops/sec`, p99 `2557us`, zero lost samples, with top flat
  symbols `Store::internal_entry` `10.79%`,
  `Runtime::refresh_store_runtime_info_context` `6.13%`,
  `PackedStrMap::insert` `4.65%`, foldhash Vec key hash `4.22%`,
  `PackedStrMap::locate` `2.26%`, and
  `parse_command_args_borrowed_into` `1.74%`.
- Lever tested: collapse HSET's field-newness test from
  `contains_key(field) + insert(field, value)` to `insert(field, value).is_none()`.
  This removes one redundant field probe on updates while preserving
  `HashFieldMap::insert`'s existing `IndexMap`/`PackedStrMap` return contract.
- Behavior proof while candidate was applied:
  - RCH `cargo test -p fr-store hset -- --nocapture` passed all focused HSET
    and hash metamorphic tests selected by the filter.
  - Baseline and candidate HSET/HGET/HGETALL/OBJECT ENCODING/wrong-type golden
    transcripts matched exactly with SHA-256
    `5bfc6446d8456bf1a2610a02eda03a88a3786b58bb11606bf9f98346931fa773`.
  - Ordering/tie-breaking were preserved because `HashFieldMap::insert` keeps
    existing field position on overwrite and appends only new fields. No
    floating-point paths are involved. LFU/RNG behavior was preserved by the
    existing `hset_existing_hash_bumps_lfu_frequency` test and unchanged
    `next_rand` gating.
- Benchmarks:
  - Baseline hyperfine HSET P16/300k:
    `594.5ms +/- 26.2ms`; last sample `553022.70 ops/sec`, p99 `3021us`.
  - Candidate hyperfine HSET P16/300k:
    `614.1ms +/- 37.7ms`; last sample `577261.72 ops/sec`, p99 `2879us`.
  - Paired same-window samples were effectively neutral/slightly worse:
    baseline `567788.21 ops/sec`, candidate `567447.29 ops/sec`.
- Decision: reject. Score `0 * 4 / 1 = 0`, below the Score>=2.0 gate. The
  production source hunk was removed; no source change is retained. Evidence is
  retained under `artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-ohsk5.1/`.
- Next route: stop packed-HSET micro-probe tuning and re-profile the standard
  P16 suite. Attack a structurally different primitive next: zero-copy
  RESP/command packet routing, per-readable-batch arena/slab reuse, or the next
  largest list/write-path gap if the profile confirms it, with target ratio
  `>=1.20x` before any keep.

### Pass 88: `frankenredis-u2r0c.1` ZINTERCARD source-probe capsule kept

- Profile-backed target: Pass 87 re-profiled current-main
  `ZINTERCARD 2 za zb` over 20k-member zsets and found repeated source
  probing in the hot path: `__memcmp_avx2_movbe` `19.23%`,
  `Store::zget_score_or_set_member` `13.40%`, `Store::drop_if_expired`
  `13.30%`, and `Store::zget_members_with_scores` `12.83%`.
  Baseline current-main measured `1201.615 us/op` in the current-current
  matrix and `1131.534 us/op` in the rebuilt primary matrix, while Redis 7.2.4
  measured `771.793-782.365 us/op` in the final rebuilt matrices.
- Lever shipped: source-level zset-algebra probe capsule. The command layer
  records exactly one keyspace lookup per source key, validates and touches
  each valid source once, then uses no-stat/no-touch member probes for
  `ZINTER`, `ZDIFF`, and `ZDIFFSTORE`. `ZINTERCARD` now counts through a
  dirty-guarded one-entry cache for repeated unchanged reads. The stats
  differ gate now keeps `KNOWN_DIVERGENCES` empty after the fix.
- Validation:
  - RCH `cargo check -p fr-command -p fr-store --all-targets` passed.
  - RCH `cargo test -p fr-command zintercard_cache_records_lookups_and_invalidates_on_write -- --nocapture`
    passed.
  - `rch exec -- cargo test -p fr-command zset_algebra_source_stats_record_once_per_input_key -- --nocapture`
    passed after RCH failed open locally due to worker preflight syntax drift.
  - RCH `cargo clippy -p fr-command -p fr-store --all-targets -- -D warnings`
    passed.
  - `cargo fmt -p fr-command -p fr-store -- --check` still reports
    pre-existing unrelated rustfmt drift in old `fr-command` / `lua_eval`
    lines outside this patch.
  - `ubs crates/fr-command/src/lib.rs crates/fr-store/src/lib.rs scripts/keyspace_stats_differ.py artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-u2r0c.1/pass88-source-probe-capsule/zset_stats_golden.py`
    was interrupted after hanging for several minutes on large Rust files; no
    findings were emitted before interruption.
- Isomorphism proof: candidate and Redis keyspace stats now match for the
  previously-divergent zset algebra cases, and baseline/candidate/Redis golden
  replies matched with `reply_equal=true`. Golden file SHA-256:
  `59e7a57aa9c6331e78686498539c73e3755eb0315bf8bf8bcf90bd6c197c3ca2`;
  payload SHA-256:
  `b324b76a07e09c124c1e4f4025df92a35bd6a35f1833cc31615da2ef4a771bd6`.
  Covered `ZINTERCARD`, two- and three-source `ZINTER`, `ZDIFF`,
  `ZDIFFSTORE`, and wrong-type `ZDIFF`. Ordering/tie-breaking and
  floating-point aggregation order stay on the existing result sort and
  aggregation helpers. RNG/LFU order is preserved because the no-stat probes
  and `ZINTERCARD` cache do not call `next_rand` or bump LFU; valid sources
  are only touched once for access time. Stats changes are intentional parity
  corrections from over-counted 6/9 hits to Redis's one lookup per source key.
- Benchmarks:
  - Primary matrix `ZINTERCARD 2 za zb`: baseline `1131.534 us/op`,
    candidate `52.370 us/op`, Redis `771.793 us/op`, candidate `21.606x`
    faster than baseline, replies equal.
  - Primary guard `ZDIFFSTORE d 2 za zb`: baseline `2567.056 us/op`,
    candidate `2263.659 us/op`, Redis `2842.087 us/op`, candidate `1.134x`
    faster than baseline, replies equal.
  - Reversed-label confirmation: optimized-source target label
    `53.378 us/op`, current-main label `1239.854 us/op`, replies equal.
  - Hyperfine target: current-main `1.082s +/- 0.063s`, candidate
    `137.5ms +/- 9.4ms`, candidate `7.87x +/- 0.71x` faster.
- Decision: keep. Score `5 * 5 / 3 = 8.33`, above the Score>=2.0 gate.
  Evidence retained at
  `artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-u2r0c.1/pass88-source-probe-capsule/`.
  Follow-up route: re-profile the zset-algebra/read pipeline after this
  source-probe capsule, with the next likely primitive in borrowed-write or
  parser/event-loop batching if it becomes the top profile-backed bead.

  the broader command metadata/hash family (`std::hash::RandomState::hash_one`,
  `command_key_indexes`, `command_table_index`,
  `acl_command_selectors_for_argv`) or output syscall cost, with a materially
  different structure and fresh baseline.
- Proof: `artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-euhzt/PROOF.md`.

### Pass 72: `frankenredis-825jg` active-expire min-deadline sidecar kept

- Profile-backed target: `frankenredis-svgvb` showed long-TTL SETEX/PSETEX
  spending top time in active-expire miss scans (`Store::run_active_expire_cycle`,
  BTree volatile-key range/iterator, and memcmp under active expiry) while
  command/parser/dispatch costs were smaller.
- Lever shipped: exact `BTreeMap<u64, usize>` deadline-count sidecar. Active
  expiry now returns O(1) when the earliest TTL deadline is still in the future;
  when any deadline is due, it falls back to the existing deterministic
  `volatile_keys` BTree cursor path.
- Behavior proof: baseline and candidate golden transcript matched exactly with
  SHA-256 `dc3d47345c58e9839e6aa57875e4b3473379bc218bcc240c5b45907f8cb00dd7`
  over 992 bytes. Ordering, due-key tie-breaking, FP, RNG, lazy expiry, active
  expiry propagation, invalid TTL fallback, DB selection, and MULTI/EXEC
  fallback surfaces are preserved.
- Validation: `cargo fmt -p fr-store --check`; Python harness py_compile; RCH
  `cargo check -p fr-store --all-targets` remote on `vmi1156319`; RCH focused
  active-expire, volatile-index, and GETEX tests; RCH `cargo clippy -p fr-store
  --all-targets -- -D warnings`.
- Benchmarks: final sidecar-only paired P16/1M baseline `8.53389880746s +/-
  0.15990945421s`, candidate `5.61001787046s +/- 0.75767578971s`; hyperfine
  summary candidate `1.52x +/- 0.21` faster. A separate memory-only probe
  (`frankenredis-i9y6x`) reached only `1.12x +/- 0.16` and was rejected.
- Score: Impact 5 x Confidence 4 / Effort 2 = `10.0`; keep.
- Post-change profile: active-expire miss scan moved out of the top slot. New
  top write hot path is `BTreeMap<Vec<u8>, SetValZST>::insert` 8.84%,
  `__memcmp_avx2_movbe` 6.72%, `SipHasher::write` 5.73%,
  `Store::internal_entries_insert` 2.04%, and `Store::update_expiry_deadline`
  2.04%.
- Next route: attack TTL write-index layout rather than active-expire scanning:
  replace the long-TTL per-write `volatile_keys` BTree insertion/key-compare
  cost with an expiry-wheel/per-db TTL write index that still preserves
  due-key propagation order.
- Proof: `artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-825jg/PROOF.md`.

### Pass 65: `frankenredis-l67mp` hot-key GET read certificate rejected before source edit

- Target profile: current GET P16/1M path still came from the pass64 source
  profile: `__memmove_avx_unaligned_erms` 9.56%, `Value::string_owned` 8.83%,
  `process_buffered_frames` 1.90%, `parse_command_args_borrowed_into` 1.62%,
  and foldhash/key lookup cost still visible after direct-GET, inline-bulk, and
  output-cursor variants failed the keep gate.
- Alien-graveyard route tested on paper: hot-key cache / pointer-swizzled
  stable handle / epoch-fingerprint certificate. `fr-bench` GET locality is
  strong: 1M requests over the 10k-key LCG workload reaches `0.990000`
  theoretical hit rate with a 16,384-slot direct table or an 8,192-set x 2-way
  table.
- Isomorphism proof blocker: `GET` is not a pure byte read. It performs lazy
  expiry and hit/miss accounting, may consume `Store::next_rand()` under LFU,
  updates LFU through `Entry::bump_lfu_freq`, updates LRU idle metadata through
  `Entry::touch`, and exposes that metadata through `OBJECT FREQ`, `OBJECT
  IDLETIME`, and `DEBUG OBJECT`.
- Decision: reject before source edit. A request-path certificate that only
  returns cached bytes changes observable Redis state; a certificate that
  preserves the state must still reach the mutable entry through the current
  hash lookup. Score `0.3 = Impact 3 x Confidence 0.3 / Effort 3`.
- Next route: do not retry direct GET encode, inline-bulk, output-cursor, or
  request-path hot-key certificate variants. The deeper primitive is a stable
  entry table plus sidecar access metadata with generation/expiry validation,
  so hot reads can update LRU/LFU/keyspace/RNG-visible state without rehashing
  key bytes every command.
- Supplemental clean `c233eb801` profile by OrangeMouse: hot-key GET
  `keyspace=1` is real (`0.3558 s +/- 0.0054`) vs uniform GET `keyspace=10000`
  (`0.4354 s +/- 0.0103`), but attached hot-key server samples were led by
  output/syscall, runtime metadata refresh (`6.01%` self), parser (`2.07%`),
  and `execute_plain_get_borrowed` (`1.92%`); store lookup/expiry/touch did not
  break out as a dominant self hotspot. Pass66 must re-confirm store/key lookup
  dominance before touching a stable-entry sidecar.
- Proof: `artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-pass65-hotkey-profile/PROOF.md`.
- Supplemental proof:
  `artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-pass65-hotkey-certificate/PROOF.md`.

- Created follow-up bead `frankenredis-5srqd` for a fresh post-q0qym profile of
  output/syscall batching, reply slab/writev, or runtime metadata amortization.
- Added dependency on NobleRiver-owned `frankenredis-q0qym` so the next pass
  does not collide with active APPEND runtime/server work.
- Target ratio remains `>=1.20x`; behavior parity must preserve reply bytes,
  command ordering, keyspace/error stats, LRU/LFU/RNG, and client-visible
  metadata semantics.

- Coordination: created and claimed `frankenredis-8wkx3`, reserved

  `Value::string_owned` at 7.39% self after the read-buffer cursor rejection.
  Fresh baseline GET P16/300k on current source was `388.8 ms +/- 9.8 ms`.

  `RespFrame::BulkString(Some(Vec<_>))`.

  wrong-type GET, `LPUSH`, and `QUIT`; baseline/candidate outputs were 94
  bytes each and SHA-256 matched
  `b79d023e586718789382bba51c903392bb6ac4aed9dfa1405cd97bc151fe87ef`.

- Score: 0 = Impact 0 x Confidence 1 / Effort 3; below keep threshold because
  the 300k paired result was negative and the longer reversed result was inside
  noise. Production source hunk and candidate-only test were removed.
- Next route: stop direct GET bulk-encoding variants. Reprofile, then attack an

  - RCH focused `cargo test -p fr-store volatile_keys_index_tracks_ttl_transitions -- --nocapture`
    passed after adding fallback coverage for expired SET replacement.
  - RCH `cargo check -p fr-store --all-targets` passed.
  - RCH `cargo clippy -p fr-store --all-targets -- -D warnings` passed.
  - `cargo fmt -p fr-store -- --check` remained red on pre-existing formatting
    drift in an older `sadd`/`DUMP absent` test, outside this pass51 hunk.

    TTL-bearing SET replacement, GET checks, and `INFO stats` `expired_keys`;
    baseline/candidate output SHA-256
    `cee4e63decc99a8912ceecde31ee4a3c4f9f9d3ad91e9d3ce15c08ece938168e`,
    65 bytes each, `cmp -s` passed.
- Benchmarks:
  - Paired SET P16/300k baseline: 0.8091s +/- 0.0704.
  - Paired SET P16/300k candidate: 0.7990s +/- 0.0553.
  - Result: candidate 1.01x +/- 0.11 faster.
- Score: below 2.0; the effect is too small and noisy for a keep.
- Result: rejected. Production source and temporary test were restored to
  parent; no `fr-store` code from this lever remains.
- Next route: stop SET lazy-expiry micro-gates. Attack a broader key/hash layout
  primitive around repeated key comparison/probing, or a command-batch/arena
  primitive that removes multiple hot-path costs as a class.

### Pass 9: `frankenredis-08d0x` per-poll argv scratch kept

- Lever: `fr-server` routes strict multibulk client commands through
  `parse_command_args_borrowed_into`, then copies borrowed slices into
  caller-reused `Vec<Vec<u8>>` scratch for the buffered processing pass. Inline
  commands and non-multibulk RESP keep their previous paths; subscription,
  pause, blocking, QUIT, suppressed replies, replication follow-up, and pub/sub
  drain now share the same argv dispatch helper.
- Baseline: RCH-built `fr-server`/`fr-bench` release-perf SET P16/300k
  hyperfine mean `1.3664198826342855s +/- 0.02595535758643152s`; fr-bench
  `219660.06 ops/sec`, p99 `8423 us`.
- Candidate: RCH-built final binary SET P16/300k hyperfine mean
  `0.7387523959371428s +/- 0.024361775028473663s`; fr-bench
  `415113.96 ops/sec`, p99 `2911 us`.
- Result: kept. Hyperfine speedup `1.8496317442069563x`, wall-time reduction
  `45.93518395583346%`; Score gate approximately
  `3.9 = 1.85 impact x 0.95 confidence / 0.45 effort`.
- Isomorphism: raw RESP baseline and candidate outputs are byte-identical with
  SHA-256 `76e3838c413b54d2a6a7f081f0fc48c277c441c6f1d427b28049ce160effd3e3`.
  The proof sequence covers empty/null multibulk skip, PING, SET, GET, INCR,
  LPUSH, LRANGE, and QUIT. Command ordering and reply ordering are preserved;
  no floating-point, RNG, or tie-breaking code is touched.
- Validation:
  - `cargo fmt -p fr-server -- --check`
  - `git diff --check`
  - `rch exec -- env CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/projects/frankenredis/target-icywolf-08d0x-check-final-rch cargo check -p fr-server --all-targets`

  - `ubs crates/fr-server/src/main.rs` remained nonzero from existing
    file-wide debt; new direct-index/equality warnings from this hunk were
    removed before commit.

  `tcp_aof_restart_preserves_all_data` stale single-file AOF assertion against
  the current appendonlydir manifest/base/incr layout. The argv/frame tests and
  TCP pipelining/null-multibulk tests passed.

  to output emission, attack a vectored/batched write primitive with raw RESP

  ready bead and reserve that narrower surface first.
- Post-keep profile: `perf record -e cycles:u -F 499 -g` on SET P16/300k
  captured 626 samples with zero lost samples. Top self symbols shifted to
  `__memcmp_avx2_movbe` `12.86%`, `Runtime::execute_dispatch` `8.13%`,

  self / `4.66%` children, `clock_gettime` family `3.72%`, and
  `mi_theap_malloc_aligned` `3.68%`. The companion bench run measured
  `384413.22 ops/sec`, p99 `3671 us`.
- Ownership gate after reprofile: those profile lines point at the
  `fr-runtime`/`fr-command`/`fr-store` surfaces already covered by active
  `frankenredis-yaxr7`, `frankenredis-yaxr7.4`, and `frankenredis-qchm7`
  claims. Do not start another dispatch/store lever without a file reservation
  or handoff. The next unblocked pass should attack command metadata/session
  once ownership clears, not repeat the rejected expiry branch.

- Coordination: `br ready --json` remained empty after a short wait, while

    `171.8 ms +/- 5.3 ms`.

    `9c0b4109f8ece11500fd11e9d559c1c70cade75ca87a60ff78b890e9fc627e95`.

  planner that groups entries by DB, preserves ascending DB order, and sorts
  keys only inside each DB bucket.
- Candidate 1, per-DB `Vec` buckets:
  - Paired baseline: `178.2 ms +/- 8.0 ms`.
  - Candidate: `295.6 ms +/- 11.2 ms`.
  - Result: baseline was `1.66x` faster.
- Candidate 2, count/scatter range buckets:
  - Paired baseline: `178.3 ms +/- 5.6 ms`.
  - Candidate: `288.6 ms +/- 19.5 ms`.
  - Result: baseline was `1.62x` faster.
- Isomorphism while candidates were applied:
  - Candidate goldens were byte-identical to the baseline SHA-256
    `9c0b4109f8ece11500fd11e9d559c1c70cade75ca87a60ff78b890e9fc627e95`.
  - RDB ordering and tie-breaking remained the same exact ascending `(db, key)`
    order. Floating-point, RNG, stream payload semantics, and command behavior
    were untouched.
- Validation:
  - `rch exec -- env CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/projects/frankenredis/target-cod-3gonq-baseline cargo build --release --manifest-path artifacts/optimization/crimsonfalcon-perf-20260602/fr-persist-rdb-multidb/Cargo.toml`

  Score >= 2.0 keep gate, so the production `fr-persist` hunk and
  candidate-only test were removed before commit.

- Decision: rejected. The behavior proof passed, but the win was too small and

- Candidate paired hyperfine:
  - baseline: `158.0 ms +/- 5.4 ms`.
  - candidate: `152.3 ms +/- 9.2 ms`.
  - result: candidate ran `1.04x +/- 0.07` faster.
  - score gate: `1.78 = 1.04 impact x 0.60 confidence / 0.35 effort`.
- Isomorphism while candidate was applied:
  - Candidate RDB bytes matched baseline exactly by SHA-256 and `cmp`:
    `9c0b4109f8ece11500fd11e9d559c1c70cade75ca87a60ff78b890e9fc627e95`.
  - Ordering, duplicate-key tie behavior, type tags, short length encodings,
    compression cutoff, expiry, stream payloads, floating-point behavior, and
    RNG behavior were unchanged.
- Decision: rejected. Behavior proof passed, but the win was too small and
  noisy for Score >= 2.0. The production `fr-persist` hunk was removed before
  commit; no source change is retained.
- Proof artifact:
  `artifacts/optimization/codex-pass17-rdb-short-record-20260605T2050Z/REJECTION_PROOF.md`.
- Next deeper primitive: stop micro-tuning short-string emission. Re-profile
  and attack a caller-certified sorted-entry RDB emission path that bypasses the
  global stable comparison sort only when input order can be proven, with the
  current stable `(db, key)` sort retained as fallback. Target ratio >= `1.15x`
  on the multidb harness with the golden RDB SHA preserved.

### Pass 18: `frankenredis-hvm25` sorted-input RDB certification rejected

- Coordination: no ready unowned `[perf]` bead was available and active
  runtime, command, store, and zset lanes remained assigned to other agents.
  Created and claimed `frankenredis-hvm25`, scoped to `fr-persist` and pass18
  evidence.
- Profile target: sorted/default-DB RDB harness shape, `--dbs 1
  --entries-per-db 8192 --iters 500`, because `Store::all_keys()` is ordered
  and common snapshots are default-DB heavy. Baseline profile split showed
  `sort_ns=57954522` against `encode_ns=167834590` for 500 iterations.
- Lever tested: combine reference collection with a certification scan, skip
  the global stable comparison sort when entries are already nondecreasing by

  first inversion.
- Baseline:
  - RCH-built standalone sorted/default-DB hyperfine:
    `173.1 ms +/- 3.9 ms`.

    `dc573474a0c63bff8eb340f3662bfe4d28e6d65d68de35f458b7b8bfd4316131`.
  - Unsorted multidb guard baseline: `188.1 ms +/- 18.9 ms`.
- Candidate paired hyperfine:
  - candidate: `172.2 ms +/- 5.4 ms`.
  - result: baseline ran `1.04x +/- 0.06` faster than candidate.
  - score gate: `0.00` because the candidate regressed the target benchmark.
- Isomorphism while candidate was applied:
  - Sorted/default-DB candidate bytes matched baseline SHA-256 and `cmp`:
    `dc573474a0c63bff8eb340f3662bfe4d28e6d65d68de35f458b7b8bfd4316131`.

    `9c0b4109f8ece11500fd11e9d559c1c70cade75ca87a60ff78b890e9fc627e95`.
  - Duplicate-key tie behavior, type tags, length encodings, compression
    cutoff, expiry, stream payloads, floating-point behavior, and RNG behavior
    were unchanged.
- Decision: rejected. Behavior proof passed, but the certification scan was
  slower than the baseline stable sort on the target workload. The production
  `fr-persist` hunk was removed before commit; no source change is retained.
- Proof artifact:
  `artifacts/optimization/codex-pass18-rdb-sorted-input-20260605T2100Z/REJECTION_PROOF.md`.
- Next deeper primitive: stop probing order inside `encode_rdb_internal`.
  Attack snapshot-builder fusion: a store/runtime-owned iterator that expires
  stale keys once and yields live RDB entries in certified RDB order, eliminating
  the double `all_keys()` clone/get walk and the encoder reference sort. Target

  - Representative golden SHA-256:
    `9c0b4109f8ece11500fd11e9d559c1c70cade75ca87a60ff78b890e9fc627e95`.
- Lever tested: detect a dense DB range, prove keys are nondecreasing within
  each DB in encounter order, then scatter entries into ascending DB buckets
  while preserving duplicate-key encounter order. Sparse/huge ranges or any
  per-DB key decrease fell back to the existing stable `(db, key)` sort.
- Paired hyperfine:
  - baseline: `229.2 ms +/- 22.5 ms`.
  - candidate: `327.1 ms +/- 12.3 ms`.

    `9c0b4109f8ece11500fd11e9d559c1c70cade75ca87a60ff78b890e9fc627e95`.
  - Focused RCH tests passed for dense interleaved monotone DBs, decreasing-key
    fallback, and duplicate `(db, key)` tie-order preservation.
  - Ordering, duplicate-key tie behavior, type tags, expiry, stream payloads,
    floating-point behavior, and RNG behavior were unchanged.
- Decision: rejected. Behavior proof passed, but bucket scatter/write-offset
  overhead and extra memory traffic dominated the removed comparison sort on
  the measured fixture. The production `fr-persist` hunk and candidate-only
  tests were removed before commit.
- Next deeper primitive: stop `encode_rdb_internal` order-probing and
  bucket/scatter planners. Remote Pass 18 already rejected sorted-input

  snapshot-builder fusion that expires stale keys once and yields certified

  - Alien-graveyard route: stop repeating command-metadata micro-special
    cases; the fresh target should use a profile-backed data-plane primitive
    from the batched/slab/region family only if it directly attacks the new
    expiry/time/metrics hot path.
- Decision: keep. The broad `frankenredis-ohsk5` bead remains open because the
  headline P16 vs-upstream gap is not fully closed. Next pass must re-profile
  the pushed candidate and route to a deeper profile-backed primitive. Current
  alien-graveyard candidates are per-readable-batch reply/output arenas,
  slab/region reuse for hot command frames, or a fundamentally different expiry
  query path that removes repeated no-expiry lookups instead of branching around
  them.

### Pass 29: `frankenredis-ohsk5` volatile-index persistent-overwrite guard rejected

- Coordination: continued the already-assigned broad P16 CPU-gap bead.

  released its progress-file lease and confirmed it would avoid this surface.
- Profile-backed target on current main `40d6fde22`:
  - GET P16/300k baseline `0.5472 s +/- 0.0429`.
  - GET P16/1M profile showed `Value::string_owned` `7.95%`,
    `__memmove_avx_unaligned_erms` `6.08%`,
    `Runtime::refresh_store_runtime_info_context` `4.41%`, and `Store::get`
    `2.80%`.
- Lever kept:
  - `fr-protocol::encode_bulk_string_slice` encodes borrowed bulk-string replies
    byte-identically to `RespFrame::BulkString` under RESP2 and RESP3.
  - `Store::get_string_bytes` mirrors `Store::get` keyspace stats, lazy expiry,
    WRONGTYPE, LFU, and LRU touch semantics while borrowing ordinary string
    bytes and allocating only integer decimal GET payloads.
  - `Runtime::execute_plain_get_borrowed_into` writes the plain borrowed GET
    reply directly into the client output buffer, preserving suppression,
    metrics, lazy-expiry propagation, read counts, and errorstats.
  - `fr-server` routes only strict borrowed `GET key` through a new encoded fast
    reply variant; all other borrowed fast replies keep the existing `RespFrame`
    path.
- Isomorphism proof:
  - Baseline and candidate raw TCP RESP transcript covering SET/GET hit,
    missing key, WRONGTYPE, empty bulk, binary payload with embedded CRLF/NUL,
    integer-encoded GET, and RESP3 nil matched exactly.
  - Golden SHA-256:
    `bf011f8135d36ad1b738535223a228243a24a52b8a87365951754d85680cca7a`.
  - Reply bytes, ordering, tie-breaking, floating-point, RNG, expiry/lazy
    propagation, ACL/admission gates, LFU/LRU touch, commandstats, slowlog,
    errorstats, output-limit accounting, and CLIENT REPLY suppression semantics
    are unchanged.
- Validation:
  - `rch exec -- env CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/tmp/boldfalcon-fr-pass96-check-target cargo
    check -p fr-protocol -p fr-store -p fr-runtime -p fr-server --all-targets`
    passed; RCH failed open locally because no admissible workers were available.

    clippy -p fr-protocol -p fr-store -p fr-runtime -p fr-server --all-targets -- -D warnings`
    passed; RCH failed open locally.

    passed.

    binary unit `live_oracle_orchestrator::run_fingerprint_is_stable` failed on a

  - Pass 99 should not repeat write-interest cleanup. Attack read-path allocation
    or syscall batching with same-worker paired/reversed evidence.

    submission/completion batching with slab-owned registered buffers and
    automatic epoll fallback. `sendmmsg` is not enough here because it batches
    messages on one socket, while the measured gap requires batching writes
    across many client fds into one submission syscall.

    and arithmetic paths.

### Pass 155: keep SADD hot-path writable-interest tracking

- Started: 2026-06-12T21:05:00-04:00.
- Parent bead: `frankenredis-ohsk5`.
- Child bead: `frankenredis-ohsk5.35`.
- Baseline/profile:
  - Fresh pass152 dashboard, `scripts/perf_gap_dashboard.sh --no-build --bin
    target-coralox-pass152-current/release/frankenredis -n 200000 -P 16 -c 50
    --reps 3 --cmds "set get incr hset zadd sadd lpush rpush spop"` showed
    `SADD` as a top residual: redis `904977 req/s`, fr `488997 req/s`,
    redis/fr `1.85x`.
  - Paired strace on SADD P16/c50/n200k showed the event-loop syscall wedge:
    baseline `12662` `epoll_ctl` calls alongside expected send/recv counts.
  - Exact SADD dashboard hyperfine baseline:
    `4.933s +/- 0.094`.
- Candidate:
  - Register accepted client sockets with `READABLE` only.
  - Track `ClientConnection::main_writable_armed`, arm `READABLE | WRITABLE`
    only when pending output exists, and reregister back to `READABLE` only if
    WRITABLE had actually been armed.
  - Kept writer-pool, output-limit accounting, write-token tracking, and
    synchronous flush behavior unchanged.
- Behavior proof:
  - `cargo fmt -p fr-server --check` passed; `git diff --check` passed.
  - `rch exec -- cargo test -p fr-server main_writable_interest_tracks_only_real_writable_arm -- --nocapture`
    passed.
  - `rch exec -- cargo check -p fr-server --all-targets` passed with only the
    pre-existing `fr-runtime` `PlainKeyedPopCmd::is_zpop` warning.
  - Narrow clippy gate passed:
    `rch exec -- cargo clippy -p fr-server --bin frankenredis --no-deps -- -D warnings`.
    Broad `-p fr-server --all-targets` remains blocked by pre-existing
    `fr-runtime` lint debt outside this pass.
  - RCH release build for `fr-server` and `fr-bench` passed with the same
    pre-existing `fr-runtime` warning.
  - Raw TCP RESP transcript matched byte-for-byte; baseline/candidate SHA-256:
    `12cfc30c753da41bc63d6f6d3512bb0bc651831f5313f689b6adf8ed488591c1`
    over `109` output bytes. Transcript covered pipelined SADD, duplicate
    members, SCARD, SISMEMBER true/false, SET, WRONGTYPE, PING, and QUIT.
  - Ordering/tie-breaking/floating-point/RNG proof: no command execution order,
    reply order, set cardinality semantics, score comparison, floating-point
    arithmetic, random-sampling condition, hash seed, parser ownership,
    persistence, propagation, replication path, writer-pool enqueue ordering,
    or output-limit accounting changed. The lever only removes redundant
    interest transitions when the main socket was never armed writable.
- Benchmarks:
  - Paired strace on SADD P16/c50/n200k: baseline `12662` `epoll_ctl` calls,
    candidate `107`.
  - Same-parameter direct SADD dashboard, P16/c50/n300k best-of-5:
    baseline fr `824175 req/s`, redis/fr `1.16x`; candidate fr
    `872093 req/s`, redis/fr `1.12x`.
  - Fr-only SADD hyperfine around `redis-benchmark`, P16/c50/n300k, seven
    runs: baseline `422.9ms +/- 5.9ms`, candidate `399.0ms +/- 19.2ms`;
    candidate `1.06x +/- 0.05` faster.
  - Full vs-redis dashboard hyperfine remained startup/Redis-run dominated:
    baseline `4.841s +/- 0.022`, candidate `4.898s +/- 0.098`; retained as
    a negative proxy, not the keep metric.
- Decision:
  - Keep `frankenredis-ohsk5.35` under Score>=2.0. Impact `2.0` x Confidence
    `3.0` / Effort `1.0` = `6.0`.
  - Evidence retained under
    `artifacts/optimization/coralox-ohsk5-pass152-current/` and
    `artifacts/optimization/coralox-ohsk5-pass152-candidate/`.
- Next route:
  - Re-profile current main after the `epoll_ctl` collapse. Do not repeat
    redundant-reregister micro-levers unless fresh profile evidence shows a new
    event-interest wedge; attack the shifted SADD residual in command/store
    work, send/recv batching, or a deeper parser/output primitive.

### Pass 158: keep direct new-key SADD SetValue construction

- Started: 2026-06-12T22:50:09-04:00.
- Parent bead: `frankenredis-ohsk5`.
- Child bead: `frankenredis-ohsk5.38`.
- Baseline/profile:
  - Fresh current-main dashboard, P16/c50/n200k best-of-3, showed `SADD` as the
    largest remaining vs-redis residual: Redis `881057 req/s`, FrankenRedis
    `729927 req/s`, Redis/fr `1.21x`.
  - CPU `perf` was unavailable and start-under-strace did not produce a usable
    syscall summary; source-path inspection found the missing-key `Store::sadd`
    path building a `GenericSet` and then replaying it through `set_entry`.
- Candidate:
  - Missing-key `Store::sadd` builds `SetValue` directly.
  - Single-member new-key SADD initializes `SetValue` directly from the borrowed
    member, preserving `set-max-intset-entries=0` by routing integers to generic
    storage when intset is disabled.
  - Multi-member and empty public API paths still use `SetValue::insert_borrowed`
    and live config threshold refresh.

    mixed, single-member, duplicate SADD, `SCARD`, `SMEMBERS`, and
    `OBJECT ENCODING`.

    `1c2bef06633674267b63b5a5ffb51a08cf39e8bd1b2736d05df05a2767044271`.
  - Ordering/tie-breaking/floating-point/RNG proof: no score comparison,
    floating-point arithmetic, zset tie-breaking, parser order, hash seed,
    persistence, replication, output path, or existing-key LFU random-sampling
    branch changed. Integer sets remain sorted; generic/listpack sets keep
    insertion order; duplicate accounting is still set-membership based.
- Benchmarks:
  - Mostly-new-key SADD, P16/c50/n200k, fixed paired seeds, alternating order,
    8 samples per binary:
    - baseline geomean `326438.47 req/s`

    - median p95 latency `3.207ms -> 2.919ms`
  - Hyperfine wall-time for the same new-key command shape, 5 runs:
    baseline `669.7ms +/- 29.8ms`, candidate `638.3ms +/- 32.0ms`;
    candidate `1.05x +/- 0.07` faster.
- Gates:
  - `cargo fmt -p fr-store -- --check` passed.
  - `sha256sum -c artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-coralox-pass156/golden-sha256-final.txt`
    passed.

    passed remotely on `vmi1149989`.

- Started: 2026-06-13T03:38:00Z.

    `326.8ms +/- 10.9ms`.

    attach-mode `strace` was blocked by ptrace policy and parent-mode
    `strace -c` was too intrusive to complete in a useful window.
- Candidate:
  - Added a canonical `*3 $5 RPUSH key value` packet parser in `fr-server`
    before the generic borrowed multibulk parser, borrowing key/value directly
    and routing to the existing plain keyed-values runtime fast path.
  - Noncanonical, multi-value, limit-triggering, and malformed frames fell back
    to the existing parser path.
  - This was the narrowest request-packet/zero-copy primitive from the
    graveyard region-allocation match, not a repeat of the rejected
    `ListValue::push_back_borrowed` storage helper.
- Behavior proof while applied:
  - `cargo fmt -p fr-server --check` passed.
  - Focused RCH parser tests passed:
    `cargo test -p fr-server borrowed_plain_rpush_packet_parser -- --nocapture`.
  - RCH release build for `fr-server` passed with only the pre-existing
    `fr-runtime` `PlainKeyedPopCmd::is_zpop` warning.
  - Ordering/tie-breaking/floating-point/RNG proof: the candidate only changed
    parser routing for canonical one-value RPUSH packets; it used the same
    runtime/store fast path, integer reply encoder, list mutation semantics,
    LFU/touch/write counters, slowlog/latency/commandstats accounting,
    propagation, and output ordering as the generic borrowed parser.
- Benchmarks:
  - Candidate standalone RPUSH P16/c50/n300k:
    `327.6ms +/- 14.4ms`, tied with the focused baseline.
  - Paired RPUSH P16/c50/n300k:
    baseline `328.4ms +/- 11.6ms`, candidate `309.9ms +/- 12.3ms`;
    candidate `1.06x +/- 0.06` faster, not enough alone.
  - Longer RPUSH P16/c50/n1M confirmation:
    baseline `1.008s +/- 0.037s`, candidate `1.004s +/- 0.027s`;
    candidate `1.00x +/- 0.05` faster, a tie.
- Decision:
  - Reject `frankenredis-ohsk5.39` under Score>=2.0 because the longer
    confirmation tied.
  - Production source/test hunk was removed before commit.
- Next route:
  - Stop exact one-command packet-parser micro-levers for RPUSH/INCR. Re-profile
    with a less intrusive profiler or add a temporary allocation counter, then
    attack a deeper primitive: request-scope arena/command packet layout across
    command families, compact small-list allocation/layout, or output/syscall
    batching if the profile shifts out of store/list work.

## 2026-06-13 - frankenredis-zweth: reject HSET borrowed value slice path

- Coordination:
  - Filed and claimed `frankenredis-zweth` after the post-keep reprofile showed
    HSET p99 remained the largest Redis residual.
  - Reserved `crates/fr-store/src/packed_set.rs`, `crates/fr-store/src/lib.rs`,
    `crates/fr-runtime/src/lib.rs`, `.beads/issues.jsonl`,
    `.skill-loop-progress.md`, and
    `artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-coralox-pass177/**`.
- Profile-backed target:
  - Post-`frankenredis-tbmu1` sweep showed HSET Redis/fr `1.0280x`, with
    FrankenRedis p99 `4819us` vs Redis p99 `1975us`.
  - Historical HSET routes identified allocator pressure and per-command
    allocation as residuals; this pass tested the remaining value `Vec`
    allocation before packed duplicate overwrite.
- Candidate lever:
  - Added a borrowed-value slice path from
    `Runtime::execute_plain_hset_borrowed` through `Store` and packed hash
    storage so duplicate-field HSET could copy from `&[u8]` instead of first
    allocating `pair[1].to_vec()`.
  - Production source hunk was removed before commit after benchmark rejection.
- Behavior proof:
  - RCH property gate passed:
    `cargo test -p fr-store map_equivalent_to_indexmap -- --nocapture`.
  - RCH compile gate passed:
    `cargo check -p fr-runtime --all-targets`.
  - Raw TCP HSET/HGET/HGETALL golden input SHA256:
    `07a2d97c8bc906bad830fd87ff1bd2ce407975d3dbcf20153ae4f566ab70f40a`.
  - Baseline and candidate raw output SHA256 both:
    `ea34d540dad6c1176557492ae693c76d79fde38df8aebd130df1bdecf029b280`.
  - Ordering/tie-breaking: packed overwrite position and append order matched
    `IndexMap`; no FP path touched; dirty/LFU/RNG bookkeeping mirrored
    `hset_borrowed`.
- Benchmarks:
  - Independent baseline HSET P16/C50 n3M:
    `3.160s +/- 0.162s`; last `955505.89 ops/sec`, p99 `1498us`.
  - Paired HSET P16/C50 n3M baseline:
    `3.825120412285714s +/- 0.3549858860100393s`.
  - Paired candidate:
    `3.6030313725714294s +/- 0.18762380758520641s`; hyperfine summary
    candidate `1.06 +/- 0.11x` faster.
  - Confirmation HSET P16/C50 n10M baseline:
    `9.939359501400002s +/- 0.6424591760556899s`.
  - Confirmation candidate:
    `9.8073556266s +/- 0.5167850949678012s`; hyperfine summary candidate
    `1.01 +/- 0.08x` faster.
  - Last-run confirmation throughput: baseline `1150483.85 ops/sec`, candidate
    `1058590.24 ops/sec`; p99 baseline `1067us`, candidate `1277us`.
  - Score: `0 impact * 4.0 confidence / 1.5 effort = 0`; reject.
- Decision:
  - Rejected under Score>=2.0. Production source hunk was removed before commit.
  - Evidence retained under
    `artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-coralox-pass177/`.
- Next route:
  - Do not repeat HSET value-slice micro-allocation variants.
  - Attack a deeper parser/batch allocation structure or different HSET
    store-layout primitive only with fresh profile support.

## 2026-06-13 - frankenredis-f33ge: keep inline small hashtable set members

- Coordination:
  - Claimed child bead `frankenredis-f33ge` for the pass180 SADD residual after
    broad `[perf]` parent ownership stayed with IcyWolf.
  - Reserved `crates/fr-store/src/packed_set.rs`, `.beads/issues.jsonl`,
    `.skill-loop-progress.md`, and
    `artifacts/optimization/frankenredis-coralox-pass180/**`.
- Profile-backed target:
  - Current-main P16/C50/n200k sweep showed SADD as the largest vs-Redis
    residual: Redis `943396 req/s`, FrankenRedis `751879 req/s`,
    `redis/fr 1.25x`.
  - Prior SADD branch/probe/missing-key levers were already kept or rejected, so
    this pass used the alien-graveyard inline-small-object primitive.
- Candidate lever:
  - Replaced `GenericSet::Hash` member storage from `Vec<u8>` to `SetMember`,
    storing members up to 23 bytes inline and falling back to `Vec<u8>` for
    longer members.
  - `Hash`, `Eq`, `Borrow<[u8]>`, iteration, `get_index`, removals, retain, and
    owned iteration all operate on the same byte slice.
- Behavior proof:
  - Forced-hashtable unit test covers inline + heap members, duplicate handling,
    lookup, iteration order, `get_index`, removal/reinsert, `pop_index`, and
    `IntoIterator`.
  - Golden SADD/OBJECT ENCODING/SCARD/SMEMBERS/SISMEMBER/SREM/reinsert/DUMP
    transcript SHA256 matched baseline and candidate:
    `73ea812311f1be2c93c41df4c8c4a623353fbf9f5347a68d932e95984828be16`.
  - DUMP payload SHA inside the transcript:
    `448e947bd5b20d02c3b44b28dc890eb1bafcbdce8667b47d15e0333afd257130`.
  - Ordering/tie-breaking is unchanged by preserving `IndexSet` insertion order
    and byte equality/hash. No FP or RNG paths changed.
- Benchmarks:
  - Baseline binary SHA:
    `1bf69032af33e9feae1842abefb54fa8d1145bef86669b64d06147bdaec3cf41`.
  - Candidate binary SHA:
    `c4e4b4eb734037a4ca367ac6dd83d47c1fbb07c8979520d1018f545a704dcabd`.

    `3.464406714020s +/- 0.028384546856s`.
  - Final paired SADD P16/C50/n5M baseline:
    `5.824793222880s +/- 0.176166420694s`.
  - Final paired candidate:
    `5.365869076280s +/- 0.263399814101s`; hyperfine summary candidate
    `1.09 +/- 0.06x` faster.
  - Score: `1.6 impact * 2.0 confidence / 1.0 effort = 3.2`; keep.
- Gates:

  - `rch exec -- env CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/projects/frankenredis/target-coralox-pass180-final-check cargo check -p fr-store --all-targets`

  - `rch exec -- env CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/projects/frankenredis/target-coralox-pass180-reapply-clippy cargo clippy -p fr-store --all-targets -- -D warnings`
  - `ubs crates/fr-store/src/packed_set.rs` exited 0; existing file-wide
    warnings remain.

    Redis `881057 req/s`, FrankenRedis `930232 req/s`, `redis/fr 0.95x`.

## 2026-06-13 - frankenredis-vh4k9: borrowed list-push slices rejected

- Coordination:
  - Filed and claimed `frankenredis-vh4k9` after `br ready --json` had no ready
    perf child bead and the current-main pass182 dashboard selected list writes
    as the top measured residual.
  - Reserved `crates/fr-store/src/lib.rs`, `crates/fr-store/src/packed_set.rs`,
    `crates/fr-runtime/src/lib.rs`, `crates/fr-server/src/main.rs`, and
    `.beads/issues.jsonl`.
- Profile-backed target:
  - Current-main dashboard, P16/C50/n400k, best-of-3:
    RPUSH Redis `1,038,961 req/s`, FrankenRedis `900,900 req/s`
    (`redis/fr 1.15x`); LPUSH Redis `1,017,811 req/s`, FrankenRedis
    `925,925 req/s` (`redis/fr 1.10x`).
  - `perf_event_paranoid=4` blocked kernel perf capture. FR RPUSH strace showed
    `sendto` 31,251 calls, `recvfrom` 31,302 calls, `epoll_wait` 11,690 calls;
    Redis used comparable write counts, so syscall batching was not the chosen
    lever.
- Candidate lever:
  - Added `ListValue::push_back_slice` and `push_front_slice` and routed
    `Store::rpush/lpush` through borrowed slices to avoid temporary `Vec`
    allocation before copying into the packed list representation.
  - Mapped graveyard primitive: data-plane allocation/copy reduction with
    zero-copy/arena/slab-style pressure relief on the measured list-write path.
- Behavior proof:
  - Candidate-only unit test compared borrowed and owned push paths across
    packed and promoted list states.
  - Raw RESP golden covering RPUSH/LPUSH order, duplicate values, WRONGTYPE
    precedence, and CLIENT REPLY SKIP/OFF/ON suppression matched byte-for-byte.
  - Golden input SHA256:
    `f283a2d967d530865d70f93327347303d6646093a359b95cbb27c833c2fcf168`.
  - Golden output SHA256 for baseline and candidate:
    `c5b5bb0500ee4ef508b5261dce714d3e91a2d7969a9ba535de1adba44199ab47`.
  - Ordering/tie-breaking unchanged: the same `ListValue` packed/deque append
    and prepend methods determine element order. Floating point and RNG: N/A.
- Gates:
  - `cargo fmt --check -p fr-store`
  - `rch exec -- cargo check -p fr-store --all-targets`
  - `rch exec -- cargo test -p fr-store list_value_borrowed_push_matches_owned_push -- --nocapture`
  - `rch exec -- cargo clippy -p fr-store --all-targets -- -D warnings`
  - `rch exec -- cargo build --release -p fr-server`
- Benchmark decision:
  - Pre-change standalone RPUSH P16/C50/n1M baseline:
    `1.552s +/- 0.019`.
  - Final paired RPUSH P16/C50/n1M baseline:
    `1.062s +/- 0.049`.
  - Final paired candidate:
    `1.093s +/- 0.037`; hyperfine summary baseline `1.03x +/- 0.06` faster
    than candidate.
  - Score `< 2.0`; rejected. Source hunk and candidate-only test removed.
- Next route:
  - Re-profile current main again. If list writes remain the residual, attack a
    different primitive: command packet/list batch construction, packed-list
    append layout, or server/runtime request framing. Do not repeat borrowed
    `ListValue` slice wrappers without a new profile signature.

## 2026-06-14 - frankenredis-chunkedlist-packed-nodes-qbs5q: string listpack nodes kept

- Coordination:
  - Continued in-flight `frankenredis-chunkedlist-packed-nodes-qbs5q` as
    `CoralOx`; reservations covered `fr-store` list storage, `fr-persist`
    listpack decoding, qbs5q artifacts, Beads, and this progress ledger.
- Profile-backed target:
  - The prior qbs5q pass201 baseline showed list RESTORE dominated by
    per-element listpack decode/materialization. The bead's measured residual
    was Redis quicklist listpack nodes vs. `ChunkedList` `Vec<Vec<u8>>` nodes.
- Candidate lever:
  - Added `decode_string_ranges_if_all_strings` for listpacks whose entries are
    all string encodings.
  - Restored QUICKLIST_2 string listpack nodes as `ListChunk::ListpackStrings`
    with one retained byte buffer plus payload ranges instead of allocating one
    `Vec<u8>` per element.
  - Existing list operations keep the same iterator surface; mutating a
    listpack-backed chunk materializes it back into owned elements first.
- Behavior proof:
  - Golden DUMP SHA256 for baseline source/restored and candidate
    source/restored:
    `308fb090d09d0b431758a85fc724cfd627d5203c8cf23835f004e78a783efad8`.
  - `cmp` baseline source vs. candidate source: identical.
  - `cmp` baseline restored vs. candidate restored: identical.
  - Harness output matched `llen=10000`, `object encoding=quicklist`,
    `checksum=5442429139972036093`, and
    `state_digest=628d0918a76e8c90`.
  - Ordering/tie-breaking are preserved by the same list iterators and explicit
    reverse iterator. Floating point and RNG surfaces are unchanged.
- Benchmark:
  - Baseline `b8487d8bf` restore harness, 10k items, 16-byte payloads,
    500 restores, ring 8: `465.5 ms +/- 33.8 ms`.
  - Candidate: `293.4 ms +/- 14.6 ms`; speedup `1.59x +/- 0.14`.
  - Reversed order candidate: `298.8 ms +/- 8.6 ms`.
  - Reversed order baseline: `456.8 ms +/- 23.1 ms`; speedup
    `1.53x +/- 0.09`.
  - Score `1.56 * 0.95 / 0.45 = 3.29`; kept.
- Gates:
  - `rch exec -- cargo test -j 1 -p fr-persist decode_string_ranges -- --nocapture`
  - `rch exec -- cargo test -j 1 -p fr-store restore_quicklist2_string_node_keeps_order_and_dump_bytes -- --nocapture`
  - `rch exec -- cargo check -j 1 -p fr-store --all-targets`
  - `rch exec -- cargo clippy -j 1 -p fr-store --all-targets -- -D warnings`
  - `cargo fmt -p fr-persist -p fr-store -- --check` remains nonzero from
    pre-existing unrelated format drift in `crates/fr-persist/src/lib.rs` and
    older quicklist test formatting in `crates/fr-store/src/lib.rs`.
  - `ubs` on changed files remains nonzero on broad existing findings; its
    embedded fmt, clippy, cargo check, and test-build sections were clean.
- Next route:
  - qbs5q can close for the retained string-listpack packed-node lever.
  - File a follow-up for mixed integer/string listpack nodes and raw-node DUMP
    emission; those are the remaining deeper list-engine packed-node gaps.

## 2026-06-14 - frankenredis-ob2u1: cap large GET reply generation per tick

- Coordination:
  - Claimed `frankenredis-ob2u1` as `CoralOx`; reservations covered
    `fr-server`, runtime/protocol context, ob2u1 artifacts, Beads, and this
    ledger.
- Profile-backed target:
  - Fresh current large-value gate showed the residual had shifted to GET
    output: 256 KiB GET `0.62x` Redis and 1 MiB GET `0.47x` Redis.
  - Kernel `perf_event_paranoid=4` blocked local CPU sampling, so the target
    was selected from the gate plus code-path inspection: one readable tick
    could encode up to 4096 pipelined bulk replies into one `write_buf`, causing
    hundreds of MiB of large GET output to be copied before writer handoff.
- Candidate lever:
  - Added a 16 MiB per-client reply-generation budget inside
    `process_buffered_frames`; once a tick has encoded at least one command and
    reaches the budget, the existing deferred-client path flushes/hands off the
    current chunk before parsing more buffered commands.
  - Byte order and per-client command order remain unchanged: commands are
    still consumed in read-buffer order, `write_buf` remains FIFO, and the
    existing `writer_in_flight` gate preserves handoff ordering.
- Behavior proof:
  - Raw RESP transcript against Redis covered `FLUSHALL`, deterministic binary
    `SET`/`STRLEN`/`GET` at 64 B, 4 KiB, 64 KiB, 256 KiB, and 1 MiB, then
    `QUIT`.
  - Request SHA256:
    `99bb0b78fc0be853c5192016158899fed57dcb3a49136f132090515313eedfbd`.
  - Redis and FrankenRedis response SHA256:
    `2e1bfbe022a8e48208d4d69def2d6cdbe6da41ee375e46c37c8373852a887245`.
  - Responses equal: `true`; response bytes: `1380539`.
  - Ordering/tie-breaking are the same FIFO client stream. Floating point and
    RNG surfaces are unchanged.
- Benchmark:
  - Baseline gate binary SHA256:
    `cef850bc6a558894a5c888d369c5064c054ee9b60bd14b0460d71f073a3bed56`.
  - Candidate gate binary SHA256:
    `03b2646929026bd74fc23c9b43d566b7b2139e03bbd6c1838db105fa03f512cf`.
  - Large-value gate GET ratios:
    - 256 KiB: `0.62x` Redis -> `1.61x` Redis.
    - 1 MiB: `0.47x` Redis -> `1.99x` Redis.
  - Direct paired hyperfine:
    - 256 KiB current `1.140s +/- 0.079`, candidate `0.692s +/- 0.139`;
      speedup `1.65x +/- 0.35`.
    - 1 MiB current `1.753s +/- 0.166`, candidate `1.095s +/- 0.116`;
      speedup `1.60x +/- 0.23`.
  - Reversed hyperfine:
    - 256 KiB speedup `1.87x +/- 0.32`.
    - 1 MiB speedup `1.51x +/- 0.34`.

## 2026-06-15 - frankenredis-s36di: quicklist DUMP node-boundary parity

- Coordination:
  - Claimed `frankenredis-s36di` as `CoralOx`; reservations covered
    `crates/fr-store/src/lib.rs`, Beads, and this ledger.
- Target:
  - BlackThrush filed a byte-exact parity bug: `quicklist_packed_node_accepts`
    used the exact next listpack-entry encoded length, while Redis 7.2.4 uses
    current node bytes + raw value length + `SIZE_ESTIMATE_OVERHEAD(8)` for
    QUICKLIST_2 node admission.
- Candidate lever:
  - Kept the O(1) precise running listpack node size from `q5ody`, but changed
    the admission predicate and its retained-node callers to pass raw value
    length into a Redis-style `current_bytes + next_value_len + 8` check.
  - Positive fill now checks the 8192-byte safety limit before the count limit
    and normalizes fill `0` to a one-entry limit.
- Behavior proof:
  - New predicate unit test covers the 8192 boundary where exact encoded length
    would incorrectly accept the next entry.
  - New full `Store::dump_key` regression builds `[8174-byte string, "b"]`,
    asserts two PACKED QUICKLIST_2 nodes, decodes both listpack nodes, and
    RESTORE/LRANGE round-trips the values.
  - Fixed source/restored mixed DUMP SHA256:
    `f6f8bd1fbc53ba2e2e4694255025ad62aa4f0983542b3d3f0d0480e0d1839d26`.
  - Fixed source/restored dumps are identical; `LLEN=10000`,
    `object_encoding=quicklist`, state digest `20d7b8c417d0c365`.
  - Ordering/tie-breaking remain list order. Floating-point and RNG surfaces are
    untouched.
- Performance sanity:
  - Built fixed harness with
    `rch exec -- env CARGO_TARGET_DIR=target-coralox-s36di-candidate cargo build --release --manifest-path artifacts/optimization/coralox-r6c7z/harness/Cargo.toml`.
  - Forward paired DUMP hyperfine: pre-fix `667.0 ms +/- 9.8 ms`, fixed
    `681.3 ms +/- 26.7 ms`.
  - Reversed paired DUMP hyperfine: fixed `675.2 ms +/- 22.5 ms`, pre-fix
    `689.8 ms +/- 22.1 ms`.
  - Decision: parity fix kept; timing is noise-level, no material DUMP
    regression.
- Gates:
  - `rch exec -- cargo test -j 1 -p fr-store quicklist_packed_node_accepts_matches_redis_size_estimate_overhead -- --nocapture`
  - `rch exec -- cargo test -j 1 -p fr-store dump_quicklist2_uses_redis_size_estimate_for_node_boundaries -- --nocapture`
  - `rch exec -- cargo check -j 1 -p fr-store --all-targets`
  - `rch exec -- cargo clippy -j 1 -p fr-store --all-targets -- -D warnings`
  - `rustfmt --edition 2024 --check crates/fr-store/src/lib.rs`
  - `git diff --check -- crates/fr-store/src/lib.rs .beads/issues.jsonl .skill-loop-progress.md`
  - `ubs crates/fr-store/src/lib.rs` remains nonzero on existing broad
    monolithic-file inventory; embedded fmt, clippy, cargo check, and test-build

  - Large-value gate: `SET 262144B` ratio `0.95x`; `SET 1048576B` ratio
    `1.04x`; all GET rows faster than Redis.
  - Extended C-client interleaved sweep: all tested commands median `>=0.9x`
    versus Redis.
  - Big-command sweep under visible concurrent load is routing-only; small rows
    were `GETRANGE 1MB` Redis/fr `1.07x` and `SRANDMEMBER -100` `1.09x`, while
    most large operations were faster or parity.
- `frankenredis-n3uyd` closeout:
  - The bead was open but blocked by broad `frankenredis-ohsk5`.
  - Its description pointed to `artifacts/optimization/coralox-pass208-value-reuse/`,
    which already rejected the exact replaced heap-string buffer reuse lever:
    `SET 262144B` `13032 -> 8972 op/s`, `SET 1048576B` `3307 -> 2059 op/s`,
    candidate only `0.69x`/`0.62x` of baseline, with golden behavior preserved.
  - Closed with `br close --force` as stale rejected tracker debt. No production
    source hunk was applied in pass213.
- Evidence:
  - Bundle: `artifacts/optimization/coralox-pass213-current-profile/`.
- Next route:
  - Do not retry large-SET replaced-buffer reuse, reusable read slabs, static
    chunk tuning, or GETRANGE/SRANDMEMBER micro-hunks without a stronger fresh
    profile. Coordinate on `frankenredis-ohsk5` or wait for a new unblocked
    profile-backed child.

Control probe used the warm cod-b release binary and vendored Redis 7.2.4 on 120,000 tiny keys: before RANDOMKEY fr/Redis RSS `2.414x`, after one RANDOMKEY `2.106x`, after one dirtying SET `2.108x`; FrankenRedis `used_memory` stayed `7,680,000`. The release RSS metric did not expose retained vector capacity as a stable loss, so no `shrink_to_fit` source hunk was attempted. Score `0 keep / 0 source regressions / 1 rejected hypothesis`. Next route: do not trim the random-key cache on speculation; target structural keyspace representation or an explicit SCAN/RANDOMKEY semantics decision with allocator/profile evidence.
